## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (continuous-time population dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate modeled as an ODE in time t and population size P. Classic population ecology uses density-independent and density-dependent per-capita growth laws, often expressed as dP_dt = P * f(t, P).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent growth with constant per-capita rate)
- Constant net immigration/emigration: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (exponential growth plus constant source/sink)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (linear births with crowding-driven deaths; carrying capacity emerges)
- Verhulst logistic differential equation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (self-limitation with a single stable carrying capacity)
- Theta-logistic (generalized logistic) ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P**c2) (nonlinear strength of density dependence)
- Richards-type (shape-parameter logistic) ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible sigmoidal approach to carrying capacity via exponent on density term)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - log(P)) (per-capita growth decreases linearly with log population size)
- Gompertz with time-varying environment: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 + c2 * t - log(P)) (carrying capacity or productivity drifting over time)
- Strong Allee effect (cubic) ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (low-density suppression with extinction threshold and upper carrying capacity)
- Weak Allee effect (modified logistic): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * P**2 (positive density dependence at low P without a strict threshold)
- Proportional harvesting/removal: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (harvest/mortality proportional to population size)
- Seasonally forced growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (periodic environment modulating growth rate)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Write dynamics via per-capita rate: (1 / P) * dP_dt = f(t, P); many ecological models become linear or simple functions in P (e.g., affine in P, affine in log(P)).
- Presence of a carrying capacity K is often indicated by a factor (1 - c * P**m) multiplying P, producing an equilibrium near P ≈ (1 / c)**(1/m).
- Allee effects typically appear as an additional low-density factor like (c * P - 1), yielding multiple equilibria (extinction threshold + carrying capacity).
- Gompertz-like regulation is suggested when per-capita growth declines with log(P), i.e., dP_dt contains P * log(P) terms rather than P**2 terms.
- Constant harvesting/immigration adds additive terms (±c0 or ±c0 * P) that shift equilibria and can create bistability or extinction under high removal.
- Environmental change or management trends often enter as explicit t-dependence in coefficients (c0 + c1 * t, exp(c * t), or periodic sin(c * t)) multiplying P.
- If growth accelerates at intermediate densities and decelerates near capacity, include higher-order density dependence (P**2, P**3) or exponents on P in the saturation factor.
- Separability is common: dP_dt = P * g(t) * h(P), enabling seasonal forcing g(t) without changing the density-regulation mechanism h(P).

(-1+P/a)(1-P/b)P = \left(-1 + P(\tfrac1a+\tfrac1b) - \tfrac{P^2}{ab}\right)P
= -P + (\tfrac1a+\tfrac1b)P^2 - \tfrac1{ab}P^3.
\]
So GT is exactly of the form
\[
\alpha P^{1/3} + A P + B P^2 + C P^3
\]
with \(\alpha=0.768873878858443\), and \(A,B,C\) fixed real numbers (no logs, no trig, no rationals, no \(t\)-dependence).

Therefore, any candidate can match only if it can be reduced (by setting its free constants) to a linear combination of \(P^{1/3}, P, P^2, P^3\) with no extra functional forms.

Now check candidates:

1. Has \(P^{3/2}, \sqrt P, \log(\cdot)\). Cannot eliminate \(\sqrt P\) and \(P^{3/2}\) while still producing the needed \(P^2,P^3\) terms; logs must be killed (set coefficient 0), leaving wrong basis. No.
2. Has logs and an exponential-inside-log term; can kill logs, but then only \(c1 P^{c0}+c2\). Cannot produce simultaneously \(P^{1/3},P,P^2,P^3\). No.
3. \(c0 P^{1/3} + c1 P^3 + (c2+c3+c4)P^2 + (c5+c6+c7)P\). This spans exactly \(P^{1/3},P,P^2,P^3\). Choose constants to match GT coefficients. Yes, possible.
4. Same structure as (3) but only one \(P\) coefficient: still spans \(P^{1/3},P,P^2,P^3\). Yes.
5. Same: \(P^{1/3},P,P^2,P^3\) available. Yes.
6. Same: redundant coefficients but includes \(P^{1/3},P,P^2,P^3\). Yes.
7. Same: includes \(P^{1/3},P,P^2,P^3\). Yes.
8. Rational function with denominator \(P^{4/3}c1+P\) and logs. To equal a polynomial-plus-\(P^{1/3}\) for all \(P\), denominator must cancel; no parameter choice makes this identically cancel to yield a pure polynomial + \(P^{1/3}\) without introducing singular/extra structure. No.
9. Rational with denominator \(Pc1+1\) and logs. Same issue: cannot become a plain polynomial + \(P^{1/3}\) for all \(P\). No.
10. Has \(t\)-dependent exponential term \(P^{c4}c5 e^{c6 t}\) and constant \(c7\). To remove \(t\), set \(c5=0\) or \(c6=0\); then expression is \(P^3,P^2,P\) plus constant, but lacks \(P^{1/3}\) and has an unavoidable constant unless \(c7=0\). Still cannot create \(P^{1/3}\). No.
11. Has correct \(P^{1/3}\) and polynomial terms, but also an extra \(P^{c5}c6 e^{Pc7}e^{c8 t}\). Must set \(c6=0\) to remove it, then remaining is \(P^{1/3}+P^3+P^2+P\). Yes.
12. Polynomial plus \(P^{c5}c6\) and constant. Could set \(c6=0\) and \(c7=0\), but then no \(P^{1/3}\). If keep \(P^{c5}\) to mimic \(P^{1/3}\), then still missing the separate fixed \(P^{1/3}\) coefficient while also needing \(P^3,P^2,P\); actually you could set \(c5=1/3\) and use \(c6\) as that coefficient, but the rest is only \(P^3,P^2,P\) which is fine. However candidate has no independent \(P^{1/3}\) term besides \(P^{c5}c6\), which is sufficient. So it *can* represent \(\alpha P^{1/3}+AP+BP^2+CP^3\) by choosing \(c5=1/3\), \(c6=\alpha\), and matching \(c0,c1,c2,c3,c4\), with \(c7=0\). Yes.
13. Has \(P^{1/3}\) and polynomial terms plus constant \(c5\). Set \(c5=0\). Then matches basis. Yes.
14. Same as 13 with extra \(P\) and constant. Set constant \(c6=0\); combine \(P\) coefficients. Yes.
15. Terms: \(P^3, P^2, P\cdot P^{c3} = P^{1+c3}\), plus \(P\) terms. No \(P^{1/3}\) unless \(1+c3=1/3\Rightarrow c3=-2/3\), but then that term is \(P^{1/3}\) multiplied by \(P\)? Actually \(P*P^{c3}=P^{1+c3}\), so yes could make \(P^{1/3}\). But then you still need a plain \(P\) term and \(P^2\) and \(P^3\), which are available. So choose \(c3=-2/3\) and \(c4\) as \(\alpha\), and match others. Yes.
16. Has \(\sqrt P\), logs, sine. To match GT, must kill log and sine terms and \(\sqrt P\) term; then only \(P c1 + c2\), missing \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\). No.
17. Has \(P^{3/2}\) and \(P^{c6}\) plus polynomial. To avoid \(P^{3/2}\), set its coefficient 0. Then can set \(c6=1/3\) to get \(P^{1/3}\) and match \(P,P^2,P^3\). Yes.
18. Has \(P^{1/3}\) and polynomial, but also \(P*c7*t\) (explicit \(t\)). Must set \(c7=0\). Then remaining includes \(P^{1/3}\), \(P^3\), \(P^2\), \(P\), plus a \(P\log(\cdot)\) term that must be killed by setting \(c5=0\). Then matches. Yes.
19. Has \(P\) plus \(P^{c1}\) plus constant and \(\log(|P|)\,|P|^{c6}\). To match for all real \(P\), absolute value/log structure cannot equal a polynomial+\(P^{1/3}\) globally. Even restricting to \(P>0\), the log term must be killed, leaving only \(P\) and \(P^{c1}\) and constant: cannot produce \(P^2,P^3\). No.
20. Has \(\sqrt P\) and log and constant; even if kill log and constant and sqrt, left with polynomial without \(P^{1/3}\). No.
21. Similar to 20. No.
22. Has \(P^{1/3}\), polynomial, plus \(P\log(\cdot)\) term. Set its coefficient \(c6=0\). Then matches. Yes.
23. Has \(\sqrt P\) and \(P^{3/2}\) and constant. Kill those by setting coefficients 0, but then left with \(P^3,P^2,P\) only, missing \(P^{1/3}\). No.
24. Has \(P^{1/3}\), polynomial, plus \(P\cdot P^{c4}=P^{1+c4}\). Set \(c5=0\) to remove that term (or set \(c4\) so it duplicates an existing power, but unnecessary). Then matches. Yes.
25. Has \(P^{1/3}\), polynomial, plus \(\log(\exp(\cdot)+1)\) term. Must set \(c5=0\). Then matches. Yes.
26. Has \(t\)-dependent exponentials and no \(P^{1/3}\) unless via \(P^{c4}\) term, but that term is multiplied by \(e^{c6 t}\). To remove \(t\), set \(c5=0\), then no \(P^{1/3}\). Alternatively set \(c6=0\) so \(e^{c6 t}=1\), but still have extra \(c7 e^{c8 t}\) unless \(c7=0\) or \(c8=0\). If set \(c7=0\) and \(c6=0\), then you have \(P^{c4}c5\) available: set \(c4=1/3\) to get \(P^{1/3}\). Then polynomial terms match. Yes.
27. Has \(t\) term \(c7 t\) and constant \(c8\). Must set \(c7=0,c8=0\). Also has \(P^{c5}c6\) which can be set to 0 (or used redundantly). Remaining matches. Yes.
28. Has sine(log(exp(P...)+1)) term; must set its coefficient \(c5=0\). Then matches. Yes.
29. Has \(\sqrt P\), logs, and \(1/\sqrt P\) via log term divided by sqrt. Cannot become polynomial+\(P^{1/3}\) for all \(P\). No.
30. Has logs and \(1/\sqrt P\). No.
31. Polynomial plus \(P^{c4}c5\) plus constant and log. Kill log and constant; set \(c4=1/3\) to supply \(P^{1/3}\). Yes.
32. Has extra \(e^{Pc6}\log(|P|)\) term; cannot equal polynomial+\(P^{1/3}\) unless coefficient 0. Set \(c5=0\) then matches. Yes.
33. Has \(P^{1/3}\), polynomial, plus \(P^{c5}\log(\cdot)\). Must set \(c6=0\) to remove that whole term. Then matches. Yes.
34. Has rational term \(P^2 c0/(P+c1)\) and logs. Even killing logs, rational term cannot equal a polynomial for all \(P\) unless it reduces to linear (e.g., \(c1=0\Rightarrow c0 P\)), but then you lose needed \(P^2,P^3\) structure and still no \(P^{1/3}\). No.

39. Has trig in \(t\). Must set trig coefficient \(c5=0\). Then matches. Yes.
40. Has \(t\)-dependent exponential*sin term; set \(c5=0\). Then matches. Yes.
41. Has \(t\)-dependent cosine term and no \(P^{1/3}\) unless via \(P^{c4}\) but it’s multiplied by \(\cos(c6 t)\). To remove \(t\), set \(c5=0\), then no \(P^{1/3}\). No.
42. Has \(P^{c0}\) and \(P^{c2}\log(\cdot)\) plus constants/logs. Kill log terms leaves \(c1 P^{c0}+c5\), cannot produce all required powers. No.
43. Has exponentials in \(P\) and \(t\) inside log; cannot reduce to polynomial+\(P^{1/3}\) except by killing those terms, leaving \(Pc0+c1\), insufficient. No.

51. Has logs and exp(sin(log)) term; killing them leaves \(c1 P^{c0}+c2\), insufficient. No.
